<p><i><b>Mylo Xyloto</b></i> <span class="nowrap"><span class="IPA nopopups"><a href="/wiki/Help:IPA_for_English" title="Help:IPA for English">/<span style="border-bottom:1px dotted"><span title="/ˈ/ primary stress follows">ˈ</span><span title="'m' in 'my'">m</span><span title="/aɪ/ long 'i' in 'tide'">aɪ</span><span title="'l' in 'lie'">l</span><span title="/oʊ/ long 'o' in 'code'">oʊ</span></span> <span style="border-bottom:1px dotted"><span title="/ˈ/ primary stress follows">ˈ</span><span title="'z' in 'Zion'">z</span><span title="/aɪ/ long 'i' in 'tide'">aɪ</span><span title="'l' in 'lie'">l</span><span title="/ə/ 'a' in 'about'">ə</span><span title="'t' in 'tie'">t</span><span title="/oʊ/ long 'o' in 'code'">oʊ</span></span>/</a></span></span> is fifth studio album by British <a href="/wiki/Alternative_rock" title="Alternative rock">alternative rock</a> band <a href="/wiki/Coldplay" title="Coldplay">Coldplay</a>. It was first released on 19 October 2011 by <a href="/wiki/EMI" title="EMI">EMI</a>, and later worldwide on 24 October. The band collaborated closely with acclaimed producer <a href="/wiki/Brian_Eno" title="Brian Eno">Brian Eno</a> following their successful collaborations on <i><a href="/wiki/Viva_la_Vida_or_Death_and_All_His_Friends" title="Viva la Vida or Death and All His Friends">Viva la Vida or Death and All His Friends</a></i>, the band's fourth studio album.</p>
<p><i>Mylo Xyloto</i> is a <a href="/wiki/Concept_album" title="Concept album">concept album</a> and a thematic <a href="/wiki/Rock_opera" title="Rock opera">rock opera</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-concept_4-0"><a href="#cite_note-concept-4">[4]</a></sup> The album tells the story of a war against sound and colour by a supremacist government, set in the world of Silencia, an <a href="/wiki/Orwellian" title="Orwellian">Orwellian</a> society. Silencia has been overtaken by a government led by Major Minus, who controls the population through media and <a href="/wiki/Propaganda" title="Propaganda">propaganda</a>. His aim is to take sound and colour off the streets in hope to draw away "feeders", creatures that use such energy to hunt its prey. The album follows Mylo, a "silencer", a soldier in an army tasked to hunt and track down "sparkers", people who harness light and energy and use it to create sparks, comparable to <a href="/wiki/Graffiti" title="Graffiti">graffiti</a> in real life. He encounters Xyloto, the sparker most wanted by Major Minus. Through Xyloto, Mylo discovers his sparker abilities and his affiliation with the Car Kids, a major sparker faction founded by Mylo's parents, Aiko and Lela. Drummer <a href="/wiki/Will_Champion" title="Will Champion">Will Champion</a> has noted that the album is a story of the characters "falling in love and trying to escape together", with a general theme of "love conquering all".</p>
<p>Internationally, <i>Mylo Xyloto</i> charted at number one in 34 countries.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-launch_5-0"><a href="#cite_note-launch-5">[5]</a></sup> In the United Kingdom, <i>Mylo Xyloto</i> became Coldplay's fifth album to debut at number one, selling 208,000 units in its first week, and setting a one-week digital sales record with 83,000 copies sold.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-6"><a href="#cite_note-6">[6]</a></sup> <i>Mylo Xyloto</i> broke an iTunes record for digital downloads sales by selling over 500,000 digital copies in a week.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-7"><a href="#cite_note-7">[7]</a></sup> The album became the group's third to debut at number one on the US <a href="/wiki/Billboard_200" title="Billboard 200"><i>Billboard</i> 200</a>, selling 447,000 units in the first week. It was the UK's best-selling rock album of 2011, selling 908,000 copies.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-revealed_2011_8-0"><a href="#cite_note-revealed_2011-8">[8]</a></sup> As of 2013, it has sold over 8 million copies worldwide.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-9"><a href="#cite_note-9">[9]</a></sup></p>
<p><i>Mylo Xyloto</i> received positive reviews from music critics, with a score of 65/100 on <a href="/wiki/Metacritic" title="Metacritic">Metacritic</a>. While some found it to be <a href="/wiki/Overproduction_(music)" title="Overproduction (music)">overproduced</a>, others praised its uplifting tone and new <a href="/wiki/Electronic_music" title="Electronic music">electronic</a> sound. "Paradise" and "Every Teardrop Is a Waterfall" received a total of three <a href="/wiki/Grammy_Award" title="Grammy Award">Grammy Award</a> <a href="/wiki/54th_Annual_Grammy_Awards" title="54th Annual Grammy Awards">nominations in 2012</a>, while the album and "Charlie Brown" received two further <a href="/wiki/55th_Annual_Grammy_Awards" title="55th Annual Grammy Awards">Grammy nominations in 2013</a>.</p>
<p></p>

<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Background">Background</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Mylo_Xyloto&amp;action=edit&amp;section=1" title="Edit section: Background">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p>In November 2008, in an interview with <a href="/wiki/All_Headline_News" title="All Headline News">All Headline News</a>, Coldplay lead singer <a href="/wiki/Chris_Martin" title="Chris Martin">Chris Martin</a> stated that "...I don't think bands should keep going past [the age of] 33",<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-10"><a href="#cite_note-10">[10]</a></sup> but later rephrased this to say that what he meant was that they must proceed "as if it's our last, because that's the only way to proceed" in December 2008, adding that he thought the band would never split.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-guard2008_11-0"><a href="#cite_note-guard2008-11">[11]</a></sup> Bassist <a href="/wiki/Guy_Berryman" title="Guy Berryman">Guy Berryman</a>, who earlier wrote that the band will "just have to start work and see how it shapes up",<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-12"><a href="#cite_note-12">[12]</a></sup> reported that the band would return to the studio:</p>
<blockquote>
<p>We've already got lists of song ideas. We never stop writing. We go into the studio with all the best laid plans then what we end up with is not what we intended. It's just exciting to wonder what will come out the speakers in a year's time. We have very exciting things lined up. It's time to take our music down different directions and really explore other avenues.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-13"><a href="#cite_note-13">[13]</a></sup></p>
</blockquote>
<p>In one interview, Chris Martin predicted the style of the incoming album as being less dominated by <a href="/wiki/Fanfare" title="Fanfare">fanfare</a>, and featuring a more "stripped-down" sound.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-DeLuca_Comedy_14-0"><a href="#cite_note-DeLuca_Comedy-14">[14]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Studios">Studios</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Mylo_Xyloto&amp;action=edit&amp;section=2" title="Edit section: Studios">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>In November 2008, Coldplay established a recording HQ at a disused bakery in Primrose Hill, North London, where they recorded a big part of <i><a href="/wiki/Viva_la_Vida_or_Death_and_All_His_Friends" title="Viva la Vida or Death and All His Friends">Viva la Vida or Death and All His Friends</a></i>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-15"><a href="#cite_note-15">[15]</a></sup> Part of Mylo Xyloto was also recorded on the same place, however this time they used a new studio, near the original, called The Beehive. While a few overdubs and a lot of comping were recorded at The Bakery, a lot of live recording and live takes were done on the new studio.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-16"><a href="#cite_note-16">[16]</a></sup> The Beehive was described by Rik Simpson, one of the producers, as a "large room". One of the band's roadies blogged about the studio, describing it as having a "gorgeous reverb".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-17"><a href="#cite_note-17">[17]</a></sup> Still about the studio he said:</p>
<blockquote>
<p>Everywhere you go there's light streaming in. Even on a relatively gloomy British afternoon, it's noticeably bright inside. I can only imagine that this will be reflected in the new material.</p>
</blockquote>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Style_and_concept">Style and concept</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Mylo_Xyloto&amp;action=edit&amp;section=3" title="Edit section: Style and concept">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p><i>Mylo Xyloto</i> is a <a href="/wiki/Concept_album" title="Concept album">concept album</a>, according to Chris Martin, "based on a love story with a happy ending." Two protagonists living in an oppressive, dystopian, urban environment, meet one another through a gang and fall in love. Lyrically, the album is inspired by "old school American <a href="/wiki/Graffiti" title="Graffiti">graffiti</a>" and "the <a href="/wiki/White_Rose" title="White Rose">White Rose</a> Movement." Martin also said that the album was influenced by <a href="/wiki/HBO" title="HBO">HBO</a> TV series <i><a href="/wiki/The_Wire" title="The Wire">The Wire</a></i>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-DeLuca_Comedy_14-1"><a href="#cite_note-DeLuca_Comedy-14">[14]</a></sup></p>
<div class="thumb tleft">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Heavily_tagged_subway_car_in_NY.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1917" data-file-width="2900" height="145" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a3/Heavily_tagged_subway_car_in_NY.jpg/220px-Heavily_tagged_subway_car_in_NY.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a3/Heavily_tagged_subway_car_in_NY.jpg/330px-Heavily_tagged_subway_car_in_NY.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a3/Heavily_tagged_subway_car_in_NY.jpg/440px-Heavily_tagged_subway_car_in_NY.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Heavily_tagged_subway_car_in_NY.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Subway car in <a href="/wiki/New_York_City" title="New York City">New York City</a>. The 1970s <a href="/wiki/Graffiti_in_New_York_City" title="Graffiti in New York City">graffiti of the city</a> inspired the album.</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>Coldplay had stated on several occasions, long before the release, that they wanted the album to be "more acoustic" and "more intimate" than its predecessor, 2008's <i><a href="/wiki/Viva_la_Vida_or_Death_and_All_His_Friends" title="Viva la Vida or Death and All His Friends">Viva la Vida or Death and All His Friends</a></i>. The band later said they got to a point where they were trying to make two records, a stripped-down album, that started to be recorded first, along with an electric one that was already being called <i>Mylo Xyloto</i> by the band. However they later decided to combine both albums. Drummer Will Champion explained that the band realized they couldn't focus on more than one thing at once, and songs like "<a href="/wiki/Paradise_(Coldplay_song)" title="Paradise (Coldplay song)">Paradise</a>" couldn't be played in an acoustic style.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-18"><a href="#cite_note-18">[18]</a></sup> Chris Martin pointed another song as a reason too:</p>
<blockquote>
<p>We have a song called Charlie Brown, which was the centrepiece of this other record we started first. We were playing the riff on an accordion and Guy came in one morning and said, 'I'm afraid I have to put my foot down. I don't want to speak out of turn, but I will not allow this song to be played on an accordion - that has to go in with the Mylo bunch'. So then we thought — let's just make one album.</p>
</blockquote>
<p>In the end some songs composed for the acoustic album such as "Us Against the World" and "U.F.O" maintained the "stripped" approach, while others such as "Charlie Brown" changed into a new form. Songs from both records ended up on the final album, world beat elements from the predecessor <i>Viva La Vida</i> are present but the overall production of it became electronic influenced. The electro rock sound can be heard through the whole album, beginning with opening song "Hurts Like Heaven" which has synthesised sounds and vocals predominantly on <a href="/wiki/Vocoder" title="Vocoder">vocoder</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-19"><a href="#cite_note-19">[19]</a></sup> The next track, "Paradise", also shows the band stepping outside of their comfort zone and going into the new electronic territory.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-20"><a href="#cite_note-20">[20]</a></sup> Additionally, this song has an R&amp;B beat style, which is also featured on "Princess Of China". This track opens with an anxious blend of synths and guitars and then goes into an R&amp;B type beat. The album has three short instrumentals which are included as noodling experimental electronic interjections on the record.</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Artwork">Artwork</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Mylo_Xyloto&amp;action=edit&amp;section=4" title="Edit section: Artwork">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:132px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:MYLO_XYLOTO.png"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="261" data-file-width="285" height="119" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7c/MYLO_XYLOTO.png/130px-MYLO_XYLOTO.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7c/MYLO_XYLOTO.png/195px-MYLO_XYLOTO.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7c/MYLO_XYLOTO.png/260px-MYLO_XYLOTO.png 2x" width="130"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:MYLO_XYLOTO.png" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
The typeface created for the album's artwork</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>The album's artworks were revealed on 12 August 2011,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-21"><a href="#cite_note-21">[21]</a></sup> inspired on graffiti the band worked again with longtime collaborators <a href="/wiki/Tappin_Gofton" title="Tappin Gofton">Tappin Gofton</a> and, this time, also with British street artist, Paris. The band had already started to research and work with graffiti on their home studios, The Bakery and The Beehive, when designer Misty Buckley introduced Paris to them, as they were looking for a graffiti artist to teach them the techniques to do it. Although initially he was supposed to be just a "teacher", Paris stayed on the project until the end, producing part of the final work along with the band.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Paris_22-0"><a href="#cite_note-Paris-22">[22]</a></sup></p>
<p>Coldplay wanted it to be an explosion of vivid colors as a counterpoint to the subdued color palette of <i>Viva La Vida</i>, and at the same time there were lots of lyrics and codes they wished to add. Researches and development into street art started six months before the work had begun.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-23"><a href="#cite_note-23">[23]</a></sup> Then a graffiti wall was painted by the band itself and Paris, formed by nine parts.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-24"><a href="#cite_note-24">[24]</a></sup> Tappin Gofton wanted the whole evolution of the wall, so at the end of every day loads of super detailed photos would be taken from it.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Paris_22-1"><a href="#cite_note-Paris-22">[22]</a></sup> In the end a picture including three parts of the wall was featured on the front cover, while the whole wall is featured on the center of the CD's booklet.</p>
<p>The final versions of the covers have a picture of the wall, half of the CD's were packed with the booklet flipped, showing the silver initials "M X" via a die-cut sheet placed over the photo on the front, while the other half was packed with the full picture and the full name of the album written over it.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-25"><a href="#cite_note-25">[25]</a></sup> Both covers use an original typeface created for this work; the new font is used in most of the album's graphic promotion.</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Title">Title</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Mylo_Xyloto&amp;action=edit&amp;section=5" title="Edit section: Title">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Chris Martin hinted at the album's title prior to release, saying it "will probably begin with an M."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-26"><a href="#cite_note-26">[26]</a></sup> During interviews the band has already given many different reasons and meanings to the album's name. In some they stated that it had no meaning and that they had had the title in mind for at least two years before deciding upon it.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-dare_27-0"><a href="#cite_note-dare-27">[27]</a></sup> But Martin also said it was reference to the album's characters, the boy (Mylo) and the girl (Xyloto) respectively.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-concept_4-1"><a href="#cite_note-concept-4">[4]</a></sup> Another meaning suggested by the frontman was that the name was supposed to be a graffiti tag for the band, relating "<a href="/wiki/Xylophone" title="Xylophone">xylophone</a>" to the word "xyloto".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-28"><a href="#cite_note-28">[28]</a></sup> Much of the art was done by Paris 1974.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Paris_22-2"><a href="#cite_note-Paris-22">[22]</a></sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Release_and_promotion">Release and promotion</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Mylo_Xyloto&amp;action=edit&amp;section=6" title="Edit section: Release and promotion">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Coldplay_Mylo_Xyloto_Tour_@_Wells_Fargo_Center.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="3456" data-file-width="5184" height="147" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0a/Coldplay_Mylo_Xyloto_Tour_%40_Wells_Fargo_Center.jpg/220px-Coldplay_Mylo_Xyloto_Tour_%40_Wells_Fargo_Center.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0a/Coldplay_Mylo_Xyloto_Tour_%40_Wells_Fargo_Center.jpg/330px-Coldplay_Mylo_Xyloto_Tour_%40_Wells_Fargo_Center.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0a/Coldplay_Mylo_Xyloto_Tour_%40_Wells_Fargo_Center.jpg/440px-Coldplay_Mylo_Xyloto_Tour_%40_Wells_Fargo_Center.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Coldplay_Mylo_Xyloto_Tour_@_Wells_Fargo_Center.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
The <a href="/wiki/Mylo_Xyloto_Tour" title="Mylo Xyloto Tour">Mylo Xyloto Tour</a> was noted for its large scale display of <a href="/wiki/Pyrotechnics" title="Pyrotechnics">pyrotechnics</a>, <a href="/wiki/Laser_lighting_display" title="Laser lighting display">laser lighting</a> and <a href="/wiki/Xyloband" title="Xyloband">Xylobands</a>. <i>(Pictured: Coldplay performing at the <a href="/wiki/Wells_Fargo_Center_(Philadelphia)" title="Wells Fargo Center (Philadelphia)">Wells Fargo Center</a> in <a href="/wiki/Philadelphia" title="Philadelphia">Philadelphia</a>, <a href="/wiki/Pennsylvania" title="Pennsylvania">Pennsylvania</a> on July 6, 2012)</i></div>
</div>
</div>
<p>The album was set to be released in December 2010 as a "decade-ender", but was postponed to 2011 since the album was far from finished as Coldplay concluded their <a href="/wiki/Viva_la_Vida_Tour" title="Viva la Vida Tour">Viva la Vida Tour</a>. Chris Martin and Jonny Buckland mentioned that the album would be released in the latter year.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (December 2011)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup></p>
<p>The <a href="/wiki/ITunes_Store" title="ITunes Store">iTunes Store</a> let users hear one new song from the album every day the week before until the album was released.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-29"><a href="#cite_note-29">[29]</a></sup></p>
<p>The album was released on 24 October 2011 on CD and on vinyl. A special edition of the album that includes the CD, digital copy and LP disc along with copies of the bands studio notes, stencils, a poster, a pop up book and stickers was made available on 19 December 2011.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-30"><a href="#cite_note-30">[30]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Singles">Singles</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Mylo_Xyloto&amp;action=edit&amp;section=7" title="Edit section: Singles">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>On 31 May, Coldplay announced that their new song "<a href="/wiki/Every_Teardrop_Is_a_Waterfall" title="Every Teardrop Is a Waterfall">Every Teardrop Is a Waterfall</a>" would be released on 3 June at 12 pm BST via download.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-31"><a href="#cite_note-31">[31]</a></sup> The single contains elements of "<a href="/wiki/I_Go_to_Rio" title="I Go to Rio">I Go to Rio</a>" written by <a href="/wiki/Peter_Allen_(musician)" title="Peter Allen (musician)">Peter Allen</a> and <a href="/wiki/Adrienne_Anderson" title="Adrienne Anderson">Adrienne Anderson</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-32"><a href="#cite_note-32">[32]</a></sup> On 21 June 2011, Coldplay's website announced that the band would release an iTunes exclusive digital EP containing the songs "Every Teardrop Is a Waterfall", "<a href="/wiki/Major_Minus" title="Major Minus">Major Minus</a>", and "<a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Moving_to_Mars_(Coldplay_song)" title="Moving to Mars (Coldplay song)">Moving to Mars</a>" on 26 June.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-33"><a href="#cite_note-33">[33]</a></sup></p>
<p>The album's second single, "<a href="/wiki/Paradise_(Coldplay_song)" title="Paradise (Coldplay song)">Paradise</a>", was released on 12 September 2011.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-34"><a href="#cite_note-34">[34]</a></sup> That same day, <a href="/wiki/Chris_Martin" title="Chris Martin">Chris Martin</a> announced that <a href="/wiki/Rihanna" title="Rihanna">Rihanna</a> would be featured on "Princess of China". "Paradise" has so far reached #15 on the <i>Billboard</i> Hot 100 chart and has reached the top 10 in 15 charts around the world. On 1 January 2012, it became the year's first number-one single in the UK and Coldplay's second chart-topper in their native country.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-dare_27-1"><a href="#cite_note-dare-27">[27]</a></sup> The song was also the best-selling rock single of 2011 in the United Kingdom, selling 410,000 copies.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-revealed_2011_8-1"><a href="#cite_note-revealed_2011-8">[8]</a></sup></p>
<p>"<a href="/wiki/Charlie_Brown_(Coldplay_song)" title="Charlie Brown (Coldplay song)">Charlie Brown</a>" was later confirmed to be the third single from the album, and the group performed the song on 23 January 2012 on the British TV series <i><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/The_X_Factor_(UK)" title="The X Factor (UK)">The X Factor</a></i>. On that date, it was solicited to US Triple A radio, and was solicited to US adult contemporary radio the following day. The single received a release date of 3 February in most other territories except for the United Kingdom, where the single was released 12 March 2012.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-35"><a href="#cite_note-35">[35]</a></sup></p>
<p>"<a href="/wiki/Princess_of_China" title="Princess of China">Princess of China</a>", a collaboration with singer <a href="/wiki/Rihanna" title="Rihanna">Rihanna</a>, was solicited to US mainstream radio on 14 February 2012 as the album's fourth single.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-36"><a href="#cite_note-36">[36]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-37"><a href="#cite_note-37">[37]</a></sup> A digital release followed on 13 April in the United States and on 4 June in the United Kingdom.</p>
<p>"<a href="/wiki/Up_with_the_Birds" title="Up with the Birds">Up with the Birds</a>" was released as a limited edition 7" vinyl single for <a href="/wiki/Record_Store_Day" title="Record Store Day">Record Store Day</a> on 21 April 2012, backed by "<a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/U.F.O._(song)" title="U.F.O. (song)">U.F.O.</a>" as its B-side.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-38"><a href="#cite_note-38">[38]</a></sup> The single, the album's fifth overall, was limited to 500 copies in the UK<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-39"><a href="#cite_note-39">[39]</a></sup> and 1,000 copies in the US.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-40"><a href="#cite_note-40">[40]</a></sup></p>
<p>"<a href="/wiki/Hurts_Like_Heaven" title="Hurts Like Heaven">Hurts Like Heaven</a>" was released as the album's sixth overall single on 27 July 2012, and was later solicited to US <a href="/wiki/Adult_album_alternative" title="Adult album alternative">Triple A</a> radio on 6 August.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-41"><a href="#cite_note-41">[41]</a></sup></p>
<p>"<a href="/wiki/Up_in_Flames_(song)" title="Up in Flames (song)">Up in Flames</a>" was released for radio airplay in Italy on 16 November 2012.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-42"><a href="#cite_note-42">[42]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Tour">Tour</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Mylo_Xyloto&amp;action=edit&amp;section=8" title="Edit section: Tour">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="hatnote" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Mylo_Xyloto_Tour" title="Mylo Xyloto Tour">Mylo Xyloto Tour</a></div>
<p>The promotion for <i>Mylo Xyloto</i> began in June with the release of the first single and the beginning of a series of performances on some of the most important festivals around the world,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-43"><a href="#cite_note-43">[43]</a></sup> including <a href="/wiki/Glastonbury_Festival_2011" title="Glastonbury Festival 2011">Glastonbury</a>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-44"><a href="#cite_note-44">[44]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/List_of_Lollapalooza_lineups_by_year#Lollapalooza" title="List of Lollapalooza lineups by year">Lollapalooza</a>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-45"><a href="#cite_note-45">[45]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Fuji_Rock_Festival" title="Fuji Rock Festival">Fuji Rock Festival</a> and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Rock_In_Rio#Rock_in_Rio_4" title="Rock In Rio">Rock In Rio</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-46"><a href="#cite_note-46">[46]</a></sup> The first time the band played live some songs from the album for a big audience was on Rock Im Park festival in Nuremberg, Germany, playing six new songs. Manager Dave Holmes said that the reason to play new songs on the festivals was to "invite people to the party" also on this he said: <i>"...let the music do the talking, play new songs and get people talking about the fact you're playing new music."</i><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-47"><a href="#cite_note-47">[47]</a></sup></p>
<p>After the "festival tour", Coldplay began the proper <a href="/wiki/Mylo_Xyloto_Tour" title="Mylo Xyloto Tour">Mylo Xyloto Tour</a> in October 2011 with a series of rehearsal concerts in Europe, as well as a special concert in <a href="/wiki/Johannesburg" title="Johannesburg">Johannesburg</a>, <a href="/wiki/South_Africa" title="South Africa">South Africa</a>, footage of which was used in the music video for "Paradise". A full-production show began in December 2011 in the United Kingdom. For this first leg, on the end of the 2011, the stage design incorporated graffiti made by the band and the band's artist Paris, it also had a catwalk linking the main stage to a smaller stage with an "X" shape. The tour continued into 2012 with shows in Europe,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-48"><a href="#cite_note-48">[48]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-49"><a href="#cite_note-49">[49]</a></sup> North America<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-50"><a href="#cite_note-50">[50]</a></sup> and Australia.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-51"><a href="#cite_note-51">[51]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Comic">Comic</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Mylo_Xyloto&amp;action=edit&amp;section=9" title="Edit section: Comic">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>On 10 July 2012 the Coldplay website announced a six-part <i>Mylo Xyloto</i> comic, with the first issue to be released at that week's <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/San_Diego_Comic-Con_International" title="San Diego Comic-Con International">San Diego Comic-Con International</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-52"><a href="#cite_note-52">[52]</a></sup> Published by <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Bongo_Comics" title="Bongo Comics">Bongo Comics</a>, the story followed the tale of Mylo, a "silencer", who, in the words of co-writer Mark Osbourne, is a part of a "war against sound and colour". Together with Osbourne, Dylan Haggerty writes the comic (starting in the second issue) with art by Alejandro Fuentes.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-53"><a href="#cite_note-53">[53]</a></sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Critical_reception">Critical reception</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Mylo_Xyloto&amp;action=edit&amp;section=10" title="Edit section: Critical reception">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>

<td style="text-align:center;vertical-align:middle"><i><a href="/wiki/Spin_(magazine)" title="Spin (magazine)">Spin</a></i></td>
<td style="text-align:center;vertical-align:middle">7/10<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-spin_64-0"><a href="#cite_note-spin-64">[64]</a></sup></td>
</tr>
</table>
<p><i>Mylo Xyloto</i> received generally positive reviews from critics, receiving a score of 65 out of 100 from review aggregator <a href="/wiki/Metacritic" title="Metacritic">Metacritic</a> based on 39 reviews, indicating "generally favorable reviews."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-mc_54-1"><a href="#cite_note-mc-54">[54]</a></sup> In a five-star review, Simon Goddard of <i><a href="/wiki/Q_(magazine)" title="Q (magazine)">Q</a></i> wrote that <i>Mylo Xyloto</i> "will, at the bare minimum, safely sustain their imperial position for a long time to come", singling out Martin and Buckland's musical contributions and Eno and Dravs' production for praise.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-q_62-1"><a href="#cite_note-q-62">[62]</a></sup> Mikael Wood of <i><a href="/wiki/Spin_(magazine)" title="Spin (magazine)">Spin</a></i> wrote that like <i><a href="/wiki/Viva_la_Vida_or_Death_and_All_His_Friends" title="Viva la Vida or Death and All His Friends">Viva la Vida or Death and All His Friends</a></i>, <i>Mylo Xyloto</i> "draws from an expansive palette that makes Coldplay's first three albums sound even quainter" and that "where <i>Viva La Vida</i> showcased Coldplay's sense of adventure, this [album] feels more eager to please".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-spin_64-1"><a href="#cite_note-spin-64">[64]</a></sup> Citing the album the band's most ambitious effort, Josh Eels of <i><a href="/wiki/Rolling_Stone" title="Rolling Stone">Rolling Stone</a></i> noted that "the choruses are bigger, the textures grander, the optimism more optimistic" and described it as a "bear-hug record for a bear-market world".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-rs_63-1"><a href="#cite_note-rs-63">[63]</a></sup> <i><a href="/wiki/The_Daily_Telegraph" title="The Daily Telegraph">The Daily Telegraph</a></i><span class="nowrap" style="padding-left:0.1em;">'</span>s Neil McCormick called the record "irresistible", noting its "adventurous" mood and "luxuriously colourful" sound.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-telegraph_57-1"><a href="#cite_note-telegraph-57">[57]</a></sup> Ian Cohen of <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Pitchfork_Media" title="Pitchfork Media">Pitchfork Media</a> wrote that the album sees the band "successfully continuing to explore the tension of wanting to be one of the best bands in the world and having to settle for being one of the biggest."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-pitchfork1_61-1"><a href="#cite_note-pitchfork1-61">[61]</a></sup></p>
<p>In a mixed review, <a href="/wiki/Alexis_Petridis" title="Alexis Petridis">Alexis Petridis</a> of <i><a href="/wiki/The_Guardian" title="The Guardian">The Guardian</a></i> judged <i>Mylo Xyloto</i><span class="nowrap" style="padding-left:0.1em;">'</span>s storyline as incoherent and expressed skepticism toward the album's purported pop influences, feeling that much of the album "just sounds like standard-issue Coldplay, replete with echoing guitars, woah-oh choruses and vocals that signify high drama by slipping into falsetto", apart from electronic music flourishes that "genuinely [add] a bit of freshness to a formulaic sound".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-guardian_59-1"><a href="#cite_note-guardian-59">[59]</a></sup> In a review for <i><a href="/wiki/Entertainment_Weekly" title="Entertainment Weekly">Entertainment Weekly</a></i>, Melissa Maerz interpreted the album as an attempt by the group to sound less like themselves in order to reconcile their commercial success with the supposed stigma of being "as hated as a band can be".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ew_58-1"><a href="#cite_note-ew-58">[58]</a></sup> Randall Roberts of the <i><a href="/wiki/Los_Angeles_Times" title="Los Angeles Times">Los Angeles Times</a></i> was critical of Martin's lyrics, stating that "every touch of lyrical bitterness is followed by enough sugar to mask the taste, which might be good in the short term but isn't a recipe for long-term health."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-latimes_65-0"><a href="#cite_note-latimes-65">[65]</a></sup></p>
<p><a href="/wiki/AllMusic" title="AllMusic">AllMusic</a> editor <a href="/wiki/Stephen_Thomas_Erlewine" title="Stephen Thomas Erlewine">Stephen Thomas Erlewine</a> wrote that <i>Mylo Xyloto</i> "has a leg up other Coldplay records for this simple reason: they're no longer attempting to mimic U2's portentous piety. They've embraced their schoolboy selves and are simply singing songs of love and good cheer, albeit on a grand scale that somehow seems smaller due to the group's insuppressible niceness."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-allmusic_55-1"><a href="#cite_note-allmusic-55">[55]</a></sup> <i><a href="/wiki/Melodic_(magazine)" title="Melodic (magazine)">Melodic</a></i> magazine's critic Johan Wippsson cited "Paradise" and "Charlie Brown" as examples of the band sounding "really on their 'own'", compared to past efforts where the band has "taken ideas from others and sometimes a little too clearly".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-melodic_66-0"><a href="#cite_note-melodic-66">[66]</a></sup> <i><a href="/wiki/Q_(magazine)" title="Q (magazine)">Q</a></i> ranked the album as the 5th best of 2011.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-67"><a href="#cite_note-67">[67]</a></sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Commercial_performance">Commercial performance</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Mylo_Xyloto&amp;action=edit&amp;section=11" title="Edit section: Commercial performance">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="thumb tleft">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Coldplay_Toronto_2011_Muchmusic.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1726" data-file-width="3213" height="118" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/f/f7/Coldplay_Toronto_2011_Muchmusic.jpg/220px-Coldplay_Toronto_2011_Muchmusic.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/f/f7/Coldplay_Toronto_2011_Muchmusic.jpg/330px-Coldplay_Toronto_2011_Muchmusic.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/f/f7/Coldplay_Toronto_2011_Muchmusic.jpg/440px-Coldplay_Toronto_2011_Muchmusic.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Coldplay_Toronto_2011_Muchmusic.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Coldplay playing in Toronto, September 2011</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>In the United Kingdom, the album sold over 122,000 copies in its first three days of sale according to <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/The_Official_Charts_Company" title="The Official Charts Company">The Official Charts Company</a>. It debuted at number one on the <a href="/wiki/UK_Albums_Chart" title="UK Albums Chart">UK Albums Chart</a> with first-week sales of over 208,000 copies, giving the band their fifth number-one album and the second-biggest first-week sales of 2011 behind <a href="/wiki/Lady_Gaga" title="Lady Gaga">Lady Gaga</a>'s <i><a href="/wiki/Born_This_Way_(album)" title="Born This Way (album)">Born This Way</a></i>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-68"><a href="#cite_note-68">[68]</a></sup> Coldplay is the third group to debut at number one with their first five albums, behind <a href="/wiki/The_Beatles" title="The Beatles">The Beatles</a> (11) and <a href="/wiki/Oasis_(band)" title="Oasis (band)">Oasis</a> (7).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-69"><a href="#cite_note-69">[69]</a></sup> The downloads accounted for 83,000 units to become the first album to sell more than 80,000 digital copies in one week, a record previously held by <a href="/wiki/Take_That" title="Take That">Take That</a>'s <i><a href="/wiki/Progress_(Take_That_album)" title="Progress (Take That album)">Progress</a></i> (79,800 units).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-70"><a href="#cite_note-70">[70]</a></sup> In its second week on the chart, the album fell to number two selling 67,132 copies.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-71"><a href="#cite_note-71">[71]</a></sup> It was the best-selling rock album in the United Kingdom, selling 908,000 copies.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-revealed_2011_8-2"><a href="#cite_note-revealed_2011-8">[8]</a></sup> The album's second single, "<a href="/wiki/Paradise_(Coldplay_song)" title="Paradise (Coldplay song)">Paradise</a>", was also the best-selling rock single in the UK, selling 410,000 copies.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-revealed_2011_8-3"><a href="#cite_note-revealed_2011-8">[8]</a></sup></p>
<p><i>Mylo Xyloto</i> debuted at number one on the <a href="/wiki/Billboard_200" title="Billboard 200"><i>Billboard</i> 200</a> in the United States, with first-week sales of 447,000 copies.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Billboard200_72-0"><a href="#cite_note-Billboard200-72">[72]</a></sup> In Canada, the album debuted at number one on the <a href="/wiki/Canadian_Albums_Chart" title="Canadian Albums Chart">Canadian Albums Chart</a>, selling 65,000 copies in its first week.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-red_hot_73-0"><a href="#cite_note-red_hot-73">[73]</a></sup> The album debuted at number one in Australia on the issue dated 31 October 2011.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ARIAChart_74-0"><a href="#cite_note-ARIAChart-74">[74]</a></sup> In its second week on the chart, the album was certified <a href="/wiki/List_of_music_recording_certifications" title="List of music recording certifications">platinum</a> by the <a href="/wiki/Australian_Recording_Industry_Association" title="Australian Recording Industry Association">Australian Recording Industry Association</a> (ARIA) for shipments of 70,000 copies.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ARIACert_75-0"><a href="#cite_note-ARIACert-75">[75]</a></sup> In Denmark, the album debuted at number two with first-week sales of 7,807 copies.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Treo_76-0"><a href="#cite_note-Treo-76">[76]</a></sup> The album was certified platinum by the <a href="/wiki/International_Federation_of_the_Phonographic_Industry" title="International Federation of the Phonographic Industry">International Federation of the Phonographic Industry</a> (IFPI) for shipments of 20,000 copies in its first week.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-revealed_2011_8-4"><a href="#cite_note-revealed_2011-8">[8]</a></sup> As of April 2014, the album has sold 1,581,000 copies in the United States.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-77"><a href="#cite_note-77">[77]</a></sup></p>

<p><b>Sample credits</b><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-credits_79-1"><a href="#cite_note-credits-79">[79]</a></sup></p>
<ul>
<li>"Every Teardrop Is a Waterfall" incorporates elements of "Ritmo De La Noche" written by <a href="/wiki/Alex_Christensen" title="Alex Christensen">Alex Christensen</a>, Harry Castioni, Bela Lagonda and Jeff Wycombe, which incorporates elements of "<a href="/wiki/I_Go_to_Rio" title="I Go to Rio">I Go to Rio</a>" written by <a href="/wiki/Peter_Allen_(musician)" title="Peter Allen (musician)">Peter Allen</a> and <a href="/wiki/Adrienne_Anderson" title="Adrienne Anderson">Adrienne Anderson</a>.</li>
<li>"Princess of China" features a sample from "<a href="/wiki/Takk..." title="Takk...">Takk...</a>" written by <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/J%C3%B3n_%C3%9E%C3%B3r_Birgisson" title="Jón Þór Birgisson">Jón Þór Birgisson</a>, <a href="/wiki/Orri_P%C3%A1ll_D%C3%BDrason" title="Orri Páll Dýrason">Orri Páll Dýrason</a>, <a href="/wiki/Georg_H%C3%B3lm" title="Georg Hólm">Georg Hólm</a> and <a href="/wiki/Kjartan_Sveinsson" title="Kjartan Sveinsson">Kjartan Sveinsson</a>, performed by <a href="/wiki/Sigur_R%C3%B3s" title="Sigur Rós">Sigur Rós</a>.</li>
<li>"Up with the Birds" features a sample from "<a href="/wiki/Driven_by_You" title="Driven by You">Driven by You</a>" by <a href="/wiki/Brian_May" title="Brian May">Brian May</a>. It also includes a lyrical sample from "Anthem" by <a href="/wiki/Leonard_Cohen" title="Leonard Cohen">Leonard Cohen</a>.</li>
</ul>
